The similar\n       <a href="/wiki/TORRO_scale" title="TORRO scale">\n        TORRO scale\n       </a>\n       ranges from a\n       <b>\n        T0\n       </b>\n       for extremely weak tornadoes to\n       <b>\n        T11\n       </b>\n       for the most powerful known tornadoes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Pulse-Doppler_radar" title="Pulse-Doppler radar">\n        Doppler\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Weather_radar" title="Weather radar">\n        radar\n       </a>\n       data,\n       <a href="/wiki/Photogrammetry" title="Photogrammetry">\n        photogrammetry\n       </a>\n       , and ground swirl patterns (cycloidal marks) may also be analyzed to determine intensity and award a rating.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EF_SPC_69-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EF_SPC-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Great_Lakes_Waterspouts.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="372" data-file-width="600" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Great_Lakes_Waterspouts.jpg/220px-Great_Lakes_Waterspouts.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Great_Lakes_Waterspouts.jpg/330px-Great_Lakes_Waterspouts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/41/Great_Lakes_Waterspouts.jpg/440px-Great_Lakes_Waterspouts.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Great_Lakes_Waterspouts.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Formation of numerous waterspouts in the\n         <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">\n          Great Lakes\n         </a>\n         region. (North America)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kings_Christian_Church_carpark_Flooded.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="895" data-file-width="1600" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Kings_Christian_Church_carpark_Flooded.jpg/220px-Kings_Christian_Church_carpark_Flooded.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Kings_Christian_Church_carpark_Flooded.jpg/330px-Kings_Christian_Church_carpark_Flooded.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Kings_Christian_Church_carpark_Flooded.jpg/440px-Kings_Christian_Church_carpark_Flooded.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kings_Christian_Church_carpark_Flooded.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A flash flood caused by a severe thunderstorm\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Waterspouts have similar characteristics as tornadoes, characterized by a spiraling funnel-shaped wind current that form over bodies of water, connecting to large cumulonimbus clouds. Waterspouts are generally classified as forms of tornadoes, or more specifically, non-\n       <a href="/wiki/Supercell" title="Supercell">\n        supercelled\n       </a>\n       tornadoes that develop over large bodies of water.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These spiralling columns of air are frequently developed within tropical areas close to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">\n        equator\n       </a>\n       , but are less common within areas of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_latitude" title="High latitude">\n        high latitude\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flash_flood">\n        Flash flood\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Flash_flood" title="Flash flood">\n        Flash flood\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Flash flooding is the process where a landscape, most notably an urban environment, is subjected to rapid floods.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These rapid floods occur more quickly and are more localized than seasonal river flooding or areal flooding\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and are frequently (though not always) associated with intense rainfall.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Flash flooding can frequently occur in slow-moving thunderstorms and is usually caused by the heavy liquid precipitation that accompanies it. Flash floods are most common in densely populated urban environments, where few plants and bodies of water are present to absorb and contain the extra water. Flash flooding can be hazardous to small infrastructure, such as bridges, and weakly constructed buildings. Plants and crops in agricultural areas can be destroyed and devastated by the force of raging water. Automobiles parked within affected areas can also be displaced.\n       <a href="/wiki/Soil" title="Soil">\n        Soil\n       </a>\n       erosion can occur as well, exposing risks of\n       <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">\n        landslide\n       </a>\n       phenomena.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Downburst">\n        Downburst\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Downburst" title="Downburst">\n        Downburst\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Downburst_damage.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Downburst_damage.jpg/220px-Downburst_damage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Downburst_damage.jpg/330px-Downburst_damage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Downburst_damage.jpg/440px-Downburst_damage.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Downburst_damage.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Trees uprooted or displaced by the force of a downburst wind in northwest Monroe County,\n         <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">\n          Wisconsin\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Downburst winds can produce numerous hazards to landscapes experiencing thunderstorms. Downburst winds are generally very powerful, and are often mistaken for wind speeds produced by tornadoes,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-erh.noaa_75-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-erh.noaa-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       due to the concentrated amount of force exerted by their straight-horizontal characteristic. Downburst winds can be hazardous to unstable, incomplete, or weakly constructed infrastructures and buildings. Agricultural crops, and other plants in nearby environments can be uprooted and damaged. Aircraft engaged in takeoff or landing can crash.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Extreme_Weather_8-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Extreme_Weather-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-erh.noaa_75-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-erh.noaa-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Automobiles can be displaced by the force exerted by downburst winds. Downburst winds are usually formed in areas when high pressure air systems of downdrafts begin to sink and displace the air masses below it, due to their higher density. When these downdrafts reach the surface, they spread out and turn into the destructive straight-horizontal winds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Extreme_Weather_8-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Extreme_Weather-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Thunderstorm_asthma">\n        Thunderstorm asthma\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorm_asthma" title="Thunderstorm asthma">\n        Thunderstorm asthma\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Thunderstorm asthma is the triggering of an asthma attack by environmental conditions directly caused by a local thunderstorm. During a thunderstorm, pollen grains can absorb moisture and then burst into much smaller fragments with these fragments being easily dispersed by wind. While larger pollen grains are usually filtered by hairs in the nose, the smaller pollen fragments are able to pass through and enter the lungs, triggering the asthma attack.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n        <a href="#cite_note-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Safety_precautions">\n        Safety precautions\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Emergency_management" title="Emergency management">\n        Emergency management\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tornado_preparedness" title="Tornado preparedness">\n        Tornado preparedness\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Most thunderstorms come and go fairly uneventfully; however, any thunderstorm can become\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Severe_thunderstorm" title="Severe thunderstorm">\n        severe\n       </a>\n       , and all thunderstorms, by definition, present the danger of\n       <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">\n        lightning\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redcross_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-redcross-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Thunderstorm preparedness and safety refers to taking steps before, during, and after a thunderstorm to minimize injury and damage.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Preparedness">\n        Preparedness\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Preparedness refers to precautions that should be taken before a thunderstorm. Some preparedness takes the form of general readiness (as a thunderstorm can occur at any time of the day or year).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS_81-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NWS-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Preparing a family emergency plan, for example, can save valuable time if a storm arises quickly and unexpectedly.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Preparing the home by removing dead or rotting limbs and trees, which can be blown over in high winds, can also significantly reduce the risk of property damage and personal injury.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fema_83-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-fema-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">\n        National Weather Service\n       </a>\n       (NWS) in the United States recommends several precautions that people should take if thunderstorms are likely to occur:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS_81-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NWS-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          Know the names of local counties, cities, and towns, as these are how warnings are described.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS_81-2">\n           <a href="#cite_note-NWS-81">\n            [81]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Monitor forecasts and weather conditions and know whether thunderstorms are likely in the area.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_84-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-84">\n            [84]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Be alert for natural signs of an approaching storm.\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Cancel or reschedule outdoor events (to avoid being caught outdoors when a storm hits).\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_84-1">\n           <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-84">\n            [84]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Take action early so you have time to get to a safe place.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_84-2">\n           <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-84">\n            [84]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Get inside a substantial building or hard-topped metal vehicle before threatening weather arrives.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_84-3">\n           <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-84">\n            [84]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          If you hear\n          <a href="/wiki/Thunder" title="Thunder">\n           thunder\n          </a>\n          , get to the safe place immediately.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_84-4">\n           <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-84">\n            [84]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Avoid open areas like hilltops, fields, and\n          <a href="/wiki/Beach" title="Beach">\n           beaches\n          </a>\n          , and don\'t be or be near the tallest objects in an area when thunderstorms are occurring.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWS_81-3">\n           <a href="#cite_note-NWS-81">\n            [81]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_84-5">\n           <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-84">\n            [84]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Don\'t shelter under tall or isolated trees during thunderstorms.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_84-6">\n           <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-84">\n            [84]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          If in the woods, put as much distance between you and any trees during thunderstorms.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_84-7">\n           <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-84">\n            [84]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          If in a group, spread out so that you increase the chances for survivors who could come to the aid of any victims from a\n          <a href="/wiki/Lightning_strike" title="Lightning strike">\n           lightning strike\n          </a>\n          .\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_84-8">\n           <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-84">\n            [84]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">\n        Safety\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       While safety and preparedness often overlap, \xe2\x80\x9cthunderstorm safety\xe2\x80\x9d generally refers to what people should do during and after a storm. The\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">\n        American Red Cross\n       </a>\n       recommends that people follow these precautions if a storm is imminent or in progress:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redcross_80-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-redcross-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          Take action immediately upon hearing thunder. Anyone close enough to the storm to hear thunder can be struck by lightning.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fema_83-1">\n           <a href="#cite_note-fema-83">\n            [83]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Avoid electrical appliances, including corded telephones.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redcross_80-2">\n           <a href="#cite_note-redcross-80">\n            [80]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <a href="/wiki/Cordless_telephone" title="Cordless telephone">\n           Cordless\n          </a>\n          and wireless telephones are safe to use during a thunderstorm.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fema_83-2">\n           <a href="#cite_note-fema-83">\n            [83]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Close and stay away from windows and doors, as glass can become a serious hazard in high wind.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redcross_80-3">\n           <a href="#cite_note-redcross-80">\n            [80]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Do not bathe or shower, as plumbing conducts\n          <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">\n           electricity\n          </a>\n          .\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          If driving, safely exit the roadway, turn on hazard lights, and park. Remain in the vehicle and avoid touching metal.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redcross_80-4">\n           <a href="#cite_note-redcross-80">\n            [80]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The NWS stopped recommending the "lightning crouch" in 2008 as it doesn\'t provide a significant level of protection and will not significantly lower the risk of being killed or injured from a nearby lightning strike.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_84-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Frequent_occurrences">\n        Frequent occurrences\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_rainfall_climatology" title="United States rainfall climatology">\n        United States rainfall climatology\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cumulonimbus_Over_Niagara_Falls.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Cumulonimbus_Over_Niagara_Falls.JPG/220px-Cumulonimbus_Over_Niagara_Falls.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Cumulonimbus_Over_Niagara_Falls.JPG/330px-Cumulonimbus_Over_Niagara_Falls.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Cumulonimbus_Over_Niagara_Falls.JPG/440px-Cumulonimbus_Over_Niagara_Falls.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cumulonimbus_Over_Niagara_Falls.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A mild thunderstorm over\n         <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Falls,_Ontario" title="Niagara Falls, Ontario">\n          Niagara Falls, Ontario\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Thunderstorms occur throughout the world, even in the polar regions, with the greatest frequency in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical" title="Tropical">\n        tropical\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">\n        rainforest\n       </a>\n       areas, where they may occur nearly daily. At any given time approximately 2,000 thunderstorms are occurring on Earth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n        <a href="#cite_note-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Kampala" title="Kampala">\n        Kampala\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tororo" title="Tororo">\n        Tororo\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">\n        Uganda\n       </a>\n       have each been mentioned as the most thunderous places on Earth,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       a claim also made for\n       <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">\n        Singapore\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Bogor" title="Bogor">\n        Bogor\n       </a>\n       on the Indonesian island of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Java_(island)" title="Java (island)">\n        Java\n       </a>\n       . Other cities known for frequent storm activity include\n       <a href="/wiki/Darwin,_Northern_Territory" title="Darwin, Northern Territory">\n        Darwin\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">\n        Caracas\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">\n        Manila\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">\n        Mumbai\n       </a>\n       . Thunderstorms are associated with the various\n       <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">\n        monsoon\n       </a>\n       seasons around the globe, and they populate the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">\n        rainbands\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">\n        tropical cyclones\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In temperate regions, they are most frequent in spring and summer, although they can occur along or ahead of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cold_front" title="Cold front">\n        cold fronts\n       </a>\n       at any time of year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DR_90-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DR-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They may also occur within a cooler air mass following the passage of a cold front over a relatively warmer body of water. Thunderstorms are rare in polar regions because of cold surface temperatures.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Some of the most powerful thunderstorms over the United States occur in the Midwest and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">\n        Southern states\n       </a>\n       . These storms can produce large hail and powerful tornadoes. Thunderstorms are relatively uncommon along much of the\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="West Coast of the United States">\n        West Coast of the United States\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but they occur with greater frequency in the inland areas, particularly the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_Valley" title="Sacramento Valley">\n        Sacramento\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_Valley" title="San Joaquin Valley">\n        San Joaquin\n       </a>\n       Valleys of\n       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">\n        California\n       </a>\n       . In spring and summer, they occur nearly daily in certain areas of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">\n        Rocky Mountains\n       </a>\n       as part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/North_American_Monsoon" title="North American Monsoon">\n        North American Monsoon\n       </a>\n       regime. In the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">\n        Northeast\n       </a>\n       , storms take on similar characteristics and patterns as the Midwest, but with less frequency and severity. During the summer,\n       <a href="/wiki/Air-mass_thunderstorm" title="Air-mass thunderstorm">\n        air-mass thunderstorms\n       </a>\n       are an almost daily occurrence over central and southern parts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">\n        Florida\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Types_of_lightning">\n        Types of lightning\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0"         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lightning_in_Arlington.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1327" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Lightning_in_Arlington.jpg/220px-Lightning_in_Arlington.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Lightning_in_Arlington.jpg/330px-Lightning_in_Arlington.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Lightning_in_Arlington.jpg/440px-Lightning_in_Arlington.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lightning_in_Arlington.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Cloud to ground lightning over\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentagon_City,_Arlington,_Virginia" title="Pentagon City, Arlington, Virginia">\n          Pentagon City\n         </a>\n         in\n         <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">\n          Arlington\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n          Virginia\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thunderstorm_in_sydney_2000x1500.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Thunderstorm_in_sydney_2000x1500.png/220px-Thunderstorm_in_sydney_2000x1500.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Thunderstorm_in_sydney_2000x1500.png/330px-Thunderstorm_in_sydney_2000x1500.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Thunderstorm_in_sydney_2000x1500.png/440px-Thunderstorm_in_sydney_2000x1500.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thunderstorm_in_sydney_2000x1500.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Lightning storm over\n         <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">\n          Sydney\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">\n        Lightning\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Lightning is an electrical discharge that occurs in a thunderstorm. It can be seen in the form of a bright streak (or bolt) from the sky. Lightning occurs when an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_charge" title="Electrical charge">\n        electrical charge\n       </a>\n       is built up within a cloud, due to static electricity generated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Supercooling" title="Supercooling">\n        supercooled\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_droplet" title="Water droplet">\n        water droplets\n       </a>\n       colliding with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ice_crystal" title="Ice crystal">\n        ice crystals\n       </a>\n       near the\n       <a href="/wiki/Freezing_level" title="Freezing level">\n        freezing level\n       </a>\n       . When a large enough charge is built up, a large discharge will occur and can be seen as lightning.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The temperature of a lightning bolt can be five times hotter than the surface of the sun.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Although the lightning is extremely hot, the duration is short and 90% of strike victims survive. Contrary to the popular idea that lightning does not strike twice in the same spot, some people have been struck by lightning over three times, and skyscrapers like the\n       <a href="/wiki/Empire_State_Building" title="Empire State Building">\n        Empire State Building\n       </a>\n       have been struck numerous times in the same storm.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The loud bang that is heard is the super heated air around the lightning bolt expanding at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_sound" title="Speed of sound">\n        speed of sound\n       </a>\n       . Because sound travels much more slowly than light the flash is seen before the bang, although both occur at the same moment.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are several types of lightning:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        In-cloud lightning is the most common. It is lightning within a cloud and is sometimes called intra-cloud or sheet lightning.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Cloud to ground lightning is when a bolt of lightning from a cloud strikes the ground. This form poses the greatest threat to life and property.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Ground to cloud lightning is when a lightning bolt is induced from the ground to the cloud.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Cloud to cloud lightning is rarely seen and is when a bolt of lightning arcs from one cloud to another.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Ball_lightning" title="Ball lightning">\n         Ball lightning\n        </a>\n        is extremely rare and has several hypothesized explanations. It is seen in the form of a 15 to 50 centimeter radius ball.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n         <a href="#cite_note-94">\n          [94]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cloud_to_air_lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cloud to air lightning (page does not exist)">\n         Cloud to air lightning\n        </a>\n        is when lightning from a cloud hits air of a different charge.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n         <a href="#cite_note-95">\n          [95]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dry_lightning" title="Dry lightning">\n         Dry lightning\n        </a>\n        is a misnomer that refers to a thunderstorm whose precipitation does not reach the ground.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heat_Lightning" title="Heat Lightning">\n         Heat Lightning\n        </a>\n        refers to a lightning flash that is seen from the horizon that does not have accompanying thunder.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n         <a href="#cite_note-96">\n          [96]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Upper-atmospheric_lightning" title="Upper-atmospheric lightning">\n         Upper-atmospheric lightning\n        </a>\n        occurs above the thunderhead.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clear-air_lightning" title="Clear-air lightning">\n         Clear-air lightning\n        </a>\n        is used widely to describe lightning that occurs with no apparent cloud close enough to have produced it. In the U.S. and\n        <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Rockies" title="Canadian Rockies">\n         Canadian Rockies\n        </a>\n        , a thunderstorm can be in an adjacent valley and not be observable, (either visually or audibly), from the valley where the lightning bolt strikes. European and Asian mountainous areas experience similar events. Also in clear areas where the storm cell is on the near horizon (within 26\xc2\xa0km (16\xc2\xa0mi) a strike can occur, and as the storm is so far away, the strike is referred to as\n        <i>\n         clear-air\n        </i>\n        .\n        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n         [\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2013)">\n            citation needed\n           </span>\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         ]\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">\n        Energy\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Sprite_(lightning)" title="Sprite (lightning)">\n        Sprite (lightning)\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Upper-atmospheric_lightning" title="Upper-atmospheric lightning">\n        Upper-atmospheric lightning\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Elmo%27s_fire" title="St. Elmo\'s fire">\n        St. Elmo\'s fire\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:How_thunderstorms_launch_particle_beams_into_space_300dpi.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3613" data-file-width="5500" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/How_thunderstorms_launch_particle_beams_into_space_300dpi.jpg/220px-How_thunderstorms_launch_particle_beams_into_space_300dpi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/How_thunderstorms_launch_particle_beams_into_space_300dpi.jpg/330px-How_thunderstorms_launch_particle_beams_into_space_300dpi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/How_thunderstorms_launch_particle_beams_into_space_300dpi.jpg/440px-How_thunderstorms_launch_particle_beams_into_space_300dpi.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:How_thunderstorms_launch_particle_beams_into_space_300dpi.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         How thunderstorms launch particle beams into space\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       If the quantity of water that is condensed in and subsequently precipitated from a cloud is known, then the total energy of a thunderstorm can be calculated. In a typical thunderstorm, approximately 5\xc3\x9710\n       <sup>\n        8\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilograms" title="Kilograms">\n        kg\n       </a>\n       of water vapor are lifted, and the amount of\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">\n        energy\n       </a>\n       released when this condenses is 10\n       <sup>\n        15\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joules" title="Joules">\n        joules\n       </a>\n       . This is on the same order of magnitude of energy released within a tropical cyclone, and more energy than that released during\n       <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">\n        the atomic bomb blast at Hiroshima, Japan in 1945\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-condensationenergy_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-condensationenergy-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fermi_Gamma-ray_Burst_Monitor" title="Fermi Gamma-ray Burst Monitor">\n        Fermi Gamma-ray Burst Monitor\n       </a>\n       results show that\n       <a href="/wiki/Gamma_ray" title="Gamma ray">\n        gamma rays\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Antimatter" title="Antimatter">\n        antimatter\n       </a>\n       particles (\n       <a href="/wiki/Positron" title="Positron">\n        positrons\n       </a>\n       ) can be generated in powerful thunderstorms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is suggested that the antimatter positrons are formed in\n       <a href="/wiki/Terrestrial_gamma-ray_flash" title="Terrestrial gamma-ray flash">\n        terrestrial gamma-ray flashes\n       </a>\n       (TGF). TGFs are brief bursts occurring inside thunderstorms and associated with lightning. The streams of positrons and electrons collide higher in the atmosphere to generate more gamma rays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       About 500 TGFs may occur every day worldwide, but mostly go undetected.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Studies">\n        Studies\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       In more contemporary times, thunderstorms have taken on the role of a scientific curiosity. Every spring,\n       <a href="/wiki/Storm_chasing" title="Storm chasing">\n        storm chasers\n       </a>\n       head to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">\n        Great Plains\n       </a>\n       of the United States and the Canadian Prairies to explore the scientific aspects of storms and tornadoes through use of videotaping.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Radio pulses produced by cosmic rays are being used to study how electric charges develop within thunderstorms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">\n        <a href="#cite_note-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       More organized meteorological projects such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VORTEX2" title="VORTEX2">\n        VORTEX2\n       </a>\n       use an array of sensors, such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Doppler_on_Wheels" title="Doppler on Wheels">\n        Doppler on Wheels\n       </a>\n       , vehicles with mounted automated\n       <a href="/wiki/Weather_station" title="Weather station">\n        weather stations\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Weather_balloon" title="Weather balloon">\n        weather balloons\n       </a>\n       , and unmanned aircraft to investigate thunderstorms expected to produce severe weather.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">\n        <a href="#cite_note-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Lightning is detected remotely using sensors that detect cloud-to-ground lightning strokes with 95\xc2\xa0percent accuracy in detection and within 250 metres (820\xc2\xa0ft) of their point of origin.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n        <a href="#cite_note-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mythology_and_religion">\n        Mythology and religion\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Thunderstorms strongly influenced many early civilizations.\n       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">\n        Greeks\n       </a>\n       believed that they were battles waged by\n       <a href="/wiki/Zeus" title="Zeus">\n        Zeus\n       </a>\n       , who hurled lightning bolts forged by\n       <a href="/wiki/Hephaestus" title="Hephaestus">\n        Hephaestus\n       </a>\n       . Some\n       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">\n        American Indian\n       </a>\n       tribes associated thunderstorms with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Thunderbird_(mythology)" title="Thunderbird (mythology)">\n        Thunderbird\n       </a>\n       , who they believed was a servant of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Spirit" title="Great Spirit">\n        Great Spirit\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n        <a href="#cite_note-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">\n        Norse\n       </a>\n       considered thunderstorms to occur when\n       <a href="/wiki/Thor" title="Thor">\n        Thor\n       </a>\n       went to fight\n       <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B6tunn" title="J\xc3\xb6tunn">\n        J\xc3\xb6tnar\n       </a>\n       , with the thunder and lightning being the effect of his strikes with the hammer\n       <a href="/wiki/Mj%C3%B6lnir" title="Mj\xc3\xb6lnir">\n        Mj\xc3\xb6lnir\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">\n        Hinduism\n       </a>\n       recognizes\n       <a href="/wiki/Indra" title="Indra">\n        Indra\n       </a>\n       as the god of rain and thunderstorms.\n       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">\n        Christian\n       </a>\n       doctrine accepted the ideas of\n       <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">\n        Aristotle\n       </a>\n       \'s original work, called\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Meteorology_(Aristotle)" title="Meteorology (Aristotle)">\n         Meteorologica\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , that winds were caused by exhalations from the Earth and that fierce storms were the work of\n       <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">\n        God\n       </a>\n       . These ideas were still within the mainstream as late as the 18th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">\n        <a href="#cite_note-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">\n        Martin Luther\n       </a>\n       was out walking when a thunderstorm began, causing him to pray to God for being saved and promising to become a monk.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Outside_of_Earth">\n        Outside of Earth\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Thunderstorms, evidenced by flashes of\n       <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">\n        lightning\n       </a>\n       , on Jupiter have been detected and are associated with clouds where water may exist as both a liquid and ice, suggesting that a similar mechanism may act as on Earth. (Water is a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polar_molecule" title="Polar molecule">\n        polar molecule\n       </a>\n       that can carry a charge, so it is capable of creating the charge separation needed to produce lightning.)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elkins-tanton_106-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-elkins-tanton-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These electrical discharges can be up to a thousand times as powerful as lightning on the Earth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">\n        <a href="#cite_note-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The water clouds can form thunderstorms driven by the heat rising from the interior.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n        <a href="#cite_note-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The clouds of Venus may also be capable of producing\n       <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">\n        lightning\n       </a>\n       ; some observations suggest that the lightning rate is at least half of that on Earth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russell2007_109-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Russell2007-109">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n
